**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# gRPC Health Checking and Keepalive Protocol Implementation

## Your Task

Find all C++ source and header files in grpc/grpc that implement the health checking service and keepalive mechanism. Identify: the health checking service implementation under src/cpp/server/health/, the keepalive timer logic in src/core/ext/transport/chttp2/, the client-side health checking channel filter, the server-side keepalive enforcement policy, and the connectivity watcher. For each file report the path and primary class or function.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grpc--v1.68.0.

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

I've successfully identified and documented all the C++ source and header files implementing the health checking service and keepalive mechanism in gRPC v1.68.0. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings:

**Health Checking Service (src/cpp/server/health/):**
- `DefaultHealthCheckService` - Main implementation class
- `HealthCheckServiceImpl` - Service implementation with WatchReactor for handling client streams
- Enable/disable functions in health_check_service.cc

**Keepalive Timer Logic (src/core/ext/transport/chttp2/transport/):**
- `grpc_chttp2_keepalive_state` enum - State machine (WAITING, PINGING, DYING, DISABLED)
- `grpc_chttp2_transport` struct - Transport with keepalive fields
- `init_keepalive_ping_locked()`, `finish_keepalive_ping_locked()` - Keepalive lifecycle functions
- `Chttp2PingRatePolicy` - Client-side ping rate enforcement
- `Chttp2PingAbusePolicy` - Server-side ping abuse detection

**Client-Side Health Checking:**
- `HealthProducer` - Creates health watch streams on subchannels
- `HealthWatcher` - Interface for load balancing policies

**Connectivity Watchers:**
- `ClientChannelFilter::ConnectivityWatcherAdder/Remover` - Channel-level watchers
- `Subchannel::ConnectedSubchannelStateWatcher` - Subchannel-level watchers
- `Server::TransportConnectivityWatcher` and `Server::ChannelData::ConnectivityWatcher` - Server-side watchers

            "content": "41: ### FAQ\n42: * When is the keepalive timer started?\n43:   * The keepalive timer is started when a transport is done connecting (after handshake).\n44: * What happens when the keepalive timer fires?\n45:   * When the keepalive timer fires, gRPC Core will try to send a keepalive ping on the transport. This ping can be blocked if -\n46:     * there is no active call on that transport and `GRPC_ARG_KEEPALIVE_PERMIT_WITHOUT_CALLS` is false.\n47:     * the number of pings already sent on the transport without any data has already exceeded `GRPC_ARG_HTTP2_MAX_PINGS_WITHOUT_DATA`.\n48:   * If a keepalive ping is not blocked and is sent on the transport, then the keepalive watchdog timer is started which will close the transport if the ping is not acknowledged before it fires.\n49: * Why am I receiving a GOAWAY with error code `ENHANCE_YOUR_CALM`?\n50: ... [chunk truncated]",
            "endLine": 57,

          {
            "content": "1: # Keepalive User Guide for gRPC Core (and dependents)\n2: \n3: The keepalive ping is a way to check if a channel is currently working by sending HTTP2 pings over the transport. It is sent periodically, and if the ping is not acknowledged by the peer within a certain timeout period, the transport is disconnected.\n4: \n5: This guide documents the knobs within gRPC core to control the current behavior of the keepalive ping.\n6: \n7: The keepalive ping in core is controlled by the following channel arguments -\n8: \n9: * **GRPC_ARG_KEEPALIVE_TIME_MS**\n10:   * This channel argument controls the period (in milliseconds) after which a keepalive ping is sent on the transport.\n11: * **GRPC_ARG_KEEPALIVE_TIMEOUT_MS**\n12:   * This channel argument controls the amount of time (in milliseconds) the sender of the keepalive ping waits for an acknowledgement. If it does not receive an acknowledgment within this time, it will close the connection.\n13: * **GRPC_ARG_HTTP2_MAX_PINGS_WITHOUT_DATA**\n14: ... [chunk truncated]",

### FAQ\\n42: * When is the keepalive timer started?\\n43:   * The keepalive timer is started when a transport is done connecting (after handshake).\\n44: * What happens when the keepalive timer fires?\\n45:   * When the keepalive timer fires, gRPC Core will try to send a keepalive ping on the transport. This ping can be blocked if -\\n46:     * there is no active call on that transport and `GRPC_ARG_KEEPALIVE_PERMIT_WITHOUT_CALLS` is false.\\n47:     * the number of pings already sent on the transport without any data has already exceeded `GRPC_ARG_HTTP2_MAX_PINGS_WITHOUT_DATA`.\\n48:   * If a keepalive ping is not blocked and is sent on the transport, then the keepalive watchdog timer is started which will close the transport if the ping is not acknowledged before it fires.\\n49: * Why am I receiving a GOAWAY with error code `ENHANCE_YOUR_CALM`?\\n50: ... [chunk truncated]\",\"endLine\":57,\"startLine\":41},{\"content\":\"1: # Keepalive User Guide for gRPC Core (and dependents)\\n2: \\n3: The keepalive ping is a way to check if a channel is currently working by sending HTTP2 pings over the transport. It is sent periodically, and if the ping is not acknowledged by the peer within a certain timeout period, the transport is disconnected.\\n4: \\n5: This guide documents the knobs within gRPC core to control the current behavior of the keepalive ping.\\n6: \\n7: The keepalive ping in core is controlled by the following channel arguments -\\n8: \\n9: * **GRPC_ARG_KEEPALIVE_TIME_MS**\\n10:   * This channel argument controls the period (in milliseconds) after which a keepalive ping is sent on the transport.\\n11: * **GRPC_ARG_KEEPALIVE_TIMEOUT_MS**\\n12:   * This channel argument controls the amount of time (in milliseconds) the sender of the keepalive ping waits for an acknowledgement. If it does not receive an acknowledgment within this time, it will close the connection.\\n13: * **GRPC_ARG_HTTP2_MAX_PINGS_WITHOUT_DATA**\\n14: ...             "content": "41: ### FAQ\n42: * When is the keepalive timer started?\n43:   * The keepalive timer is started when a transport is done connecting (after handshake).\n44: * What happens when the keepalive timer fires?\n45:   * When the keepalive timer fires, gRPC Core will try to send a keepalive ping on the transport. This ping can be blocked if -\n46:     * there is no active call on that transport and `GRPC_ARG_KEEPALIVE_PERMIT_WITHOUT_CALLS` is false.\n47:     * the number of pings already sent on the transport without any data has already exceeded `GRPC_ARG_HTTP2_MAX_PINGS_WITHOUT_DATA`.\n48:   * If a keepalive ping is not blocked and is sent on the transport, then the keepalive watchdog timer is started which will close the transport if the ping is not acknowledged before it fires.\n49: * Why am I receiving a GOAWAY with error code `ENHANCE_YOUR_CALM`?\n50: ... [chunk truncated]",
            "endLine": 57,
            "startLine": 41

          {
            "content": "1: # Keepalive User Guide for gRPC Core (and dependents)\n2: \n3: The keepalive ping is a way to check if a channel is currently working by sending HTTP2 pings over the transport. It is sent periodically, and if the ping is not acknowledged by the peer within a certain timeout period, the transport is disconnected.\n4: \n5: This guide documents the knobs within gRPC core to control the current behavior of the keepalive ping.\n6: \n7: The keepalive ping in core is controlled by the following channel arguments -\n8: \n9: * **GRPC_ARG_KEEPALIVE_TIME_MS**\n10:   * This channel argument controls the period (in milliseconds) after which a keepalive ping is sent on the transport.\n11: * **GRPC_ARG_KEEPALIVE_TIMEOUT_MS**\n12:   * This channel argument controls the amount of time (in milliseconds) the sender of the keepalive ping waits for an acknowledgement. If it does not receive an acknowledgment within this time, it will close the connection.\n13: * **GRPC_ARG_HTTP2_MAX_PINGS_WITHOUT_DATA**\n14: ... [chunk truncated]",
            "endLine": 30,
